href="/wiki/Hail" title="Hail">\n            Hail\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <a href="/wiki/Ice_pellets" title="Ice pellets">\n            Ice pellets\n           </a>\n           (\n           <a href="/wiki/Diamond_dust" title="Diamond dust">\n            Diamond dust\n           </a>\n           )\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <a href="/wiki/Rain" title="Rain">\n            Rain\n           </a>\n           (\n           <a href="/wiki/Freezing_rain" title="Freezing rain">\n            Freezing rain\n           </a>\n           )\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <a href="/wiki/Cloudburst" title="Cloudburst">\n            Cloudburst\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <a href="/wiki/Snow" title="Snow">\n            Snow\n           </a>\n           <ul>\n            <li>\n             <a href="/wiki/Rain_and_snow_mixed" title="Rain and snow mixed">\n              Rain and snow mixed\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li>\n             <a href="/wiki/Snow_grains" title="Snow grains">\n              Snow grains\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li>\n             <a href="/wiki/Snow_roller" title="Snow roller">\n              Snow roller\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li>\n             <a href="/wiki/Slush" </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">\n         <ul>\n          <li>\n           <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_river" title="Atmospheric river">\n            Atmospheric river\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_convection" title="Atmospheric convection">\n            Atmospheric convection\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">\n            Air pollution\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <a class="mw-selflink selflink">\n            Climate\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <a href="/wiki/Cloud" title="Cloud">\n            Cloud\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <a href="/wiki/Fog" title="Fog">\n            Fog\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <a href="/wiki/Cold_wave" title="Cold wave">\n            Cold wave\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <a href="/wiki/Heat_wave" title="Heat wave">\n            Heat wave\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <a href="/wiki/Jet_stream" title="Jet stream">\n            Jet stream\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <a href="/wiki/Meteorology" title="Meteorology">\n            Meteorology\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <a href="/wiki/Severe_weather" title="Severe weather">\n            Severe weather\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <a href="/wiki/Weather_forecasting" title="Weather forecasting">\n            Weather forecasting\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td style="padding:0.3em 0.4em 0.3em;font-weight:bold;border-top:#ccc 1px solid; border-bottom:#ccc 1px solid;">\n         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cumulus_clouds_in_fair_weather.jpeg">\n          <img alt="Cumulus clouds in fair weather.jpeg" class="noviewer" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Cumulus_clouds_in_fair_weather.jpeg/16px-Cumulus_clouds_in_fair_weather.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Cumulus_clouds_in_fair_weather.jpeg/24px-Cumulus_clouds_in_fair_weather.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Cumulus_clouds_in_fair_weather.jpeg/32px-Cumulus_clouds_in_fair_weather.jpeg 2x" width="16"/>\n         </a>\n         <a href="/wiki/Portal:Weather" title="Portal:Weather">\n          Weather portal\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%">\n         <div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">\n          <ul>\n           <li class="nv-view">\n            <a href="/wiki/Template:Weather" title="Template:Weather">\n             <abbr title="View this template">\n              v\n             </abbr>\n            </a>\n           </li>\n           <li class="nv-talk">\n            <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Weather" title="Template talk:Weather">\n             <abbr title="Discuss this template">\n              t\n             </abbr>\n            </a>\n           </li>\n           <li class="nv-edit">\n            <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Weather&amp;action=edit">\n             <abbr title="Edit this template">\n              e\n             </abbr>\n            </a>\n           </li>\n          </ul>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Climate\n       </b>\n       is the statistics of\n       <a href="/wiki/Weather" title="Weather">\n        weather\n       </a>\n       over long periods of time.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IPCC-2015_1-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-IPCC-2015-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20050201_2-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NASA-20050201-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It is measured by assessing the patterns of variation in\n       <a href="/wiki/Temperature" title="Temperature">\n        temperature\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Humidity" title="Humidity">\n        humidity\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_pressure" title="Atmospheric pressure">\n        atmospheric pressure\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Wind" title="Wind">\n        wind\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Precipitation" title="Precipitation">\n        precipitation\n       </a>\n       , atmospheric particle count and other\n       <a href="/wiki/Meteorology" title="Meteorology">\n        meteorological\n       </a>\n       variables in a given region over long periods of time. Climate differs from weather, in that weather only describes the short-term conditions of these variables in a given region.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A region\'s climate is generated by the\n       <b>\n        climate system\n       </b>\n       , which has five components:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Earth%27s_Atmosphere" title="Earth\'s Atmosphere">\n        atmosphere\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrosphere" title="Hydrosphere">\n        hydrosphere\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Cryosphere" title="Cryosphere">\n        cryosphere\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Lithosphere" title="Lithosphere">\n        lithosphere\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Biosphere" title="Biosphere">\n        biosphere\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IPCC_glossary_3-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-IPCC_glossary-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The climate of a location is affected by its\n       <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">\n        latitude\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Terrain" title="Terrain">\n        terrain\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Altitude" title="Altitude">\n        altitude\n       </a>\n       , as well as nearby\n       <a href="/wiki/Body_of_water" title="Body of water">\n        water bodies\n       </a>\n       and their currents. Climates can be\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_classification" title="Climate classification">\n        classified\n       </a>\n       according to the average and the typical ranges of different variables, most commonly temperature and precipitation. The most commonly used classification scheme was the\n       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">\n        K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification\n       </a>\n       . The Thornthwaite system,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       in use since 1948, incorporates\n       <a href="/wiki/Evapotranspiration" title="Evapotranspiration">\n        evapotranspiration\n       </a>\n       along with temperature and precipitation information and is used in studying biological diversity and how\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">\n        climate change\n       </a>\n       affects it. The Bergeron and\n       <a href="/wiki/Spatial_Synoptic_Classification_system" title="Spatial Synoptic Classification system">\n        Spatial Synoptic Classification systems\n       </a>\n       focus on the origin of air masses that define the climate of a region.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Paleoclimatology" title="Paleoclimatology">\n        Paleoclimatology\n       </a>\n       is the study of ancient climates. Since direct observations of climate are not available before the 19th century, paleoclimates are inferred from\n       <a href="/wiki/Proxy_(climate)" title="Proxy (climate)">\n        proxy variables\n       </a>\n       that include non-biotic evidence such as sediments found in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lake_beds" title="Lake beds">\n        lake beds\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Ice_core" title="Ice core">\n        ice cores\n       </a>\n       , and biotic evidence such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Dendrochronology" title="Dendrochronology">\n        tree rings\n       </a>\n       and coral.\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_model" title="Climate model">\n        Climate models\n       </a>\n       are mathematical models of past, present and future climates. Climate change may occur over long and short timescales from a variety of factors; recent warming is discussed in\n       <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">\n        global warming\n       </a>\n       . Global warming results in redistributions. For example, "a 3\xc2\xb0C change in mean annual temperature corresponds to a shift in isotherms of approximately 300\xe2\x80\x93400 km in latitude (in the temperate zone) or 500 m in elevation. Therefore, species are expected to move upwards in elevation or towards the poles in latitude in response to shifting climate zones".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TIEE-20000201_6-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-TIEE-20000201-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1">\n         <a href="#Definition">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           1\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n <a href="#Bergeron_and_Spatial_Synoptic">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Bergeron and Spatial Synoptic\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4">\n           <a href="#K.C3.B6ppen">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             K\xc3\xb6ppen\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5">\n           <a href="#Thornthwaite">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Thornthwaite\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6">\n         <a href="#Record">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           3\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Record\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7">\n           <a href="#Modern">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             3.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Modern\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8">\n           <a href="#Paleoclimatology">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             3.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Paleoclimatology\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9">\n         <a href="#Climate_change">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           4\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Climate change\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10">\n           <a href="#Climate_models">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             4.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Climate models\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           5\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           6\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13">\n         <a href="#Further_reading">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Further reading\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Definition">\n        Definition\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Definition">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Climate (from\n       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">\n        Ancient Greek\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        klima\n       </i>\n       , meaning\n       <i>\n        inclination\n       </i>\n       ) is commonly defined as the weather averaged over a long period.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The standard averaging period is 30\xc2\xa0years,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but other periods may be used depending on the purpose. Climate also includes statistics other than the average, such as the magnitudes of day-to-day or year-to-year variations. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">\n        Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change\n       </a>\n       (IPCC)\n       <a href="/wiki/IPCC_Third_Assessment_Report" title="IPCC Third Assessment Report">\n        2001\n       </a>\n       glossary definition is as follows:\n      </p>\n      <blockquote class="templatequote">\n       <p>\n        <i>\n         Climate in a narrow sense is usually defined as the "average weather," or more rigorously, as the statistical description in terms of the mean and variability of relevant quantities over a period ranging from months to thousands or millions of years. The classical period is 30\xc2\xa0years, as defined by the World Meteorological Organization (WMO). These quantities are most often surface variables such as temperature, precipitation, and wind. Climate in a wider sense is the state, including a statistical description, of the climate system.\n        </i>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">\n         <a href="#cite_note-9">\n          [9]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </p>\n      </blockquote>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">\n        World Meteorological Organization\n       </a>\n       (WMO) describes climate "normals" as "reference points used by climatologists to compare current climatological trends to that of the past or what is considered \'normal\'. A Normal is defined as the arithmetic average of a climate element (e.g. temperature) over a 30-year period. A 30 year period is used, as it is long enough to filter out any interannual variation or anomalies, but also short enough to be able to show longer climatic trends."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WMO_data_10-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WMO_data-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The WMO originated from the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Meteorological_Organization" title="International Meteorological Organization">\n        International Meteorological Organization\n       </a>\n       which set up a technical commission for climatology in 1929. At its 1934\n       <a href="/wiki/Wiesbaden" title="Wiesbaden">\n        Wiesbaden\n       </a>\n       meeting the technical commission designated the thirty-year period from 1901 to 1930 as the reference time frame for climatological standard normals. In 1982 the WMO agreed to update climate normals, and these were subsequently completed on the basis of climate data from 1 January 1961 to 31 December 1990.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WMO_history_11-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WMO_history-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The difference between climate and weather is usefully summarized by the popular phrase "Climate is what you expect, weather is what you get."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Over\n       <a href="/wiki/History" title="History">\n        historical\n       </a>\n       time spans there are a number of nearly constant variables that determine climate, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">\n        latitude\n       </a>\n       , altitude, proportion of land to water, and proximity to oceans and mountains. These change only over periods of millions of years due to processes such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Plate_tectonics" title="Plate tectonics">\n        plate tectonics\n       </a>\n       . Other climate determinants are more dynamic: the\n       <a href="/wiki/Thermohaline_circulation" title="Thermohaline circulation">\n        thermohaline circulation\n       </a>\n       of the ocean leads to a 5\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (9\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F) warming of the northern\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">\n        Atlantic Ocean\n       </a>\n       compared to other ocean basins.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Other\n       <a href="/wiki/Ocean_current" title="Ocean current">\n        ocean currents\n       </a>\n       redistribute heat between land and water on a more regional scale. The density and type of vegetation coverage affects solar heat absorption,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       water retention, and rainfall on a regional level. Alterations in the quantity of atmospheric\n       <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">\n        greenhouse gases\n       </a>\n       determines the amount of solar energy retained by the planet, leading to\n       <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">\n        global warming\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/Global_cooling" title="Global cooling">\n        global cooling\n       </a>\n       . The variables which determine climate are numerous and the interactions complex, but there is general agreement that the broad outlines are understood, at least insofar as the determinants of historical climate change are concerned.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ledley1999_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Ledley1999-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_classification">\n        Climate classification\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Climate classification">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ClimateMap_World.png">\n         <img alt="Map of world dividing climate zones, largely influenced by latitude. The zones, going from the equator upward (and downward) are Tropical, Dry, Moderate, Continental and Polar. There are subzones within these zones." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="470" data-file-width="727" height="259" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/ClimateMap_World.png/400px-ClimateMap_World.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/ClimateMap_World.png/600px-ClimateMap_World.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/df/ClimateMap_World.png 2x" width="400"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ClimateMap_World.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <center>\n          Worldwide climate classifications\n         </center>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       There are several ways to\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_classification" title="Climate classification">\n        classify climates\n       </a>\n       into similar regimes. Originally,\n       <a href="/wiki/Clime" title="Clime">\n        climes\n       </a>\n       were defined in\n       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">\n        Ancient Greece\n       </a>\n       to describe the weather depending upon a location\'s latitude. Modern climate classification methods can be broadly divided into\n       <i>\n        genetic\n       </i>\n       methods, which focus on the causes of climate, and\n       <i>\n        empiric\n       </i>\n       methods, which focus on the effects of climate. Examples of genetic classification include methods based on the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Relative_frequency" title="Relative frequency">\n        relative frequency\n       </a>\n       of different\n       <a href="/wiki/Air_mass" title="Air mass">\n        air mass\n       </a>\n       types or locations within\n       <a href="/wiki/Synoptic_scale_meteorology" title="Synoptic scale meteorology">\n        synoptic\n       </a>\n       weather disturbances. Examples of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Empirical" title="Empirical">\n        empiric\n       </a>\n       classifications include\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climate_zone" title="Climate zone">\n        climate zones\n       </a>\n       defined by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plant_hardiness" title="Plant hardiness">\n        plant hardiness\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       evapotranspiration,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thorn_17-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-thorn-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       or more generally the\n       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">\n        K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification\n       </a>\n       which was originally designed to identify the climates associated with certain\n       <a href="/wiki/Biome" title="Biome">\n        biomes\n       </a>\n       . A common shortcoming of these\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classification_scheme" title="Classification scheme">\n        classification schemes\n       </a>\n       is that they produce distinct boundaries between the zones they define, rather than the gradual transition of climate properties more common in nature.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Bergeron_and_Spatial_Synoptic">\n        Bergeron and Spatial Synoptic\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Bergeron and Spatial Synoptic">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Air_mass" title="Air mass">\n        Air mass\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The simplest classification is that involving air masses. The Bergeron classification is the most widely accepted form of air mass classification.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Air mass classification involves three letters. The first letter describes its\n       <a href="/wiki/Moisture" title="Moisture">\n        moisture\n       </a>\n       properties, with c used for continental air masses (dry) and m for maritime air masses (moist). The second letter describes the thermal characteristic of its source region: T for\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical" title="Tropical">\n        tropical\n       </a>\n       , P for\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polar_region" title="Polar region">\n        polar\n       </a>\n       , A for\n       <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">\n        Arctic\n       </a>\n       or Antarctic, M for\n       <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">\n        monsoon\n       </a>\n       , E for\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Equatorial_climate" title="Equatorial climate">\n        equatorial\n       </a>\n       , and S for superior air (dry air formed by significant downward motion in the atmosphere). The third letter is used to designate the stability of the atmosphere. If the air mass is colder than the ground below it, it is labeled k. If the air mass is warmer than the ground below it, it is labeled w.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       While air mass identification was originally used in\n       <a href="/wiki/Weather_forecasting" title="Weather forecasting">\n        weather forecasting\n       </a>\n       during the 1950s, climatologists began to establish synoptic climatologies based on this idea in 1973.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schwartz1995_20-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Schwartz1995-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Based upon the Bergeron classification scheme is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Spatial_Synoptic_Classification_system" title="Spatial Synoptic Classification system">\n        Spatial Synoptic Classification system\n       </a>\n       (SSC). There are six categories within the SSC scheme: Dry Polar (similar to continental polar), Dry Moderate (similar to maritime superior), Dry Tropical (similar to continental tropical), Moist Polar (similar to maritime polar), Moist Moderate (a hybrid between maritime polar and maritime tropical), and Moist Tropical (similar to maritime tropical, maritime monsoon, or maritime equatorial).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="K\xc3\xb6ppen">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="K.C3.B6ppen">\n        K\xc3\xb6ppen\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: K\xc3\xb6ppen">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MonthlyMeanT.gif">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="340" data-file-width="550" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/MonthlyMeanT.gif/220px-MonthlyMeanT.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/MonthlyMeanT.gif/330px-MonthlyMeanT.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/MonthlyMeanT.gif/440px-MonthlyMeanT.gif 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MonthlyMeanT.gif" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Monthly average surface temperatures from 1961\xe2\x80\x931990. This is an example of how climate varies with location and season\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BlueMarble_monthlies_animation.gif">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="432" data-file-width="864" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/BlueMarble_monthlies_animation.gif/220px-BlueMarble_monthlies_animation.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/BlueMarble_monthlies_animation.gif/330px-BlueMarble_monthlies_animation.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/BlueMarble_monthlies_animation.gif/440px-BlueMarble_monthlies_animation.gif 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BlueMarble_monthlies_animation.gif" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Monthly global images from NASA Earth Observatory\n         <a class="external text" href="http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5b/BlueMarble_monthlies_SMIL.svg">\n          (interactive SVG)\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">\n        K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The K\xc3\xb6ppen classification depends on average monthly values of temperature and precipitation. The most commonly used form of the K\xc3\xb6ppen classification has five primary types labeled A through E. These primary types are A) tropical, B) dry, C) mild mid-latitude, D) cold mid-latitude, and E) polar. The five primary classifications can be further divided into secondary classifications such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">\n        rainforest\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">\n        monsoon\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_savanna" title="Tropical savanna">\n        tropical savanna\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical" title="Humid subtropical">\n        humid subtropical\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Humid_continental" title="Humid continental">\n        humid continental\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">\n        oceanic climate\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">\n        Mediterranean climate\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">\n        desert\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">\n        steppe\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">\n        subarctic climate\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">\n        tundra\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Polar_ice_cap" title="Polar ice cap">\n        polar ice cap\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Rainforests\n       </b>\n       are characterized by high\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rainfall" title="Rainfall">\n        rainfall\n       </a>\n       , with definitions setting minimum normal annual rainfall between 1,750 millimetres (69\xc2\xa0in) and 2,000 millimetres (79\xc2\xa0in). Mean monthly temperatures exceed 18\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (64\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F) during all months of the year.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A\n       <b>\n        monsoon\n       </b>\n       is a seasonal prevailing wind which lasts for several months, ushering in a region\'s rainy season.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Regions within\n       <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">\n        North America\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">\n        South America\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">\n        Sub-Saharan Africa\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">\n        Australia\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_Asian_monsoon" title="East Asian monsoon">\n        East Asia\n       </a>\n       are monsoon regimes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Globalcldfr_amo_200207-201504_lrg.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1800" data-file-width="3600" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Globalcldfr_amo_200207-201504_lrg.jpg/220px-Globalcldfr_amo_200207-201504_lrg.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Globalcldfr_amo_200207-201504_lrg.jpg/330px-Globalcldfr_amo_200207-201504_lrg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Globalcldfr_amo_200207-201504_lrg.jpg/440px-Globalcldfr_amo_200207-201504_lrg.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Globalcldfr_amo_200207-201504_lrg.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The world\xe2\x80\x99s cloudy and sunny spots. NASA Earth Observatory map using data collected between July 2002 and April 2015.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n          <a href="#cite_note-25">\n           [25]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A\n       <b>\n        tropical savanna\n       </b>\n       is a\n       <a href="/wiki/Grassland" title="Grassland">\n        grassland\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Biome" title="Biome">\n        biome\n       </a>\n       located in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semiarid" title="Semiarid">\n        semiarid\n       </a>\n       to semi-\n       <a href="/wiki/Humidity" title="Humidity">\n        humid\n       </a>\n       climate regions of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subtropical" title="Subtropical">\n        subtropical\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical" title="Tropical">\n        tropical\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">\n        latitudes\n       </a>\n       , with average temperatures remain at or above 18\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (64\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F) year round and rainfall between 750 millimetres (30\xc2\xa0in) and 1,270 millimetres (50\xc2\xa0in) a year. They are widespread on\n       <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">\n        Africa\n       </a>\n       , and are found in\n       <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">\n        India\n       </a>\n       , the northern parts of\n       <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">\n        South America\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">\n        Malaysia\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">\n        Australia\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAVWOOD_26-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SAVWOOD-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:5_11_15_Brian_AquabyMonth.gif">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="360" data-file-width="720" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/5_11_15_Brian_AquabyMonth.gif/220px-5_11_15_Brian_AquabyMonth.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/5_11_15_Brian_AquabyMonth.gif/330px-5_11_15_Brian_AquabyMonth.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/5_11_15_Brian_AquabyMonth.gif/440px-5_11_15_Brian_AquabyMonth.gif 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:5_11_15_Brian_AquabyMonth.gif" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Cloud cover by month for 2014. NASA Earth Observatory\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n          <a href="#cite_note-27">\n           [27]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n          <a href="#cite_note-28">\n           [28]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <b>\n        humid subtropical\n       </b>\n       climate zone where winter rainfall (and sometimes\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Snowfall" title="Snowfall">\n        snowfall\n       </a>\n       ) is associated with large\n       <a href="/wiki/Storm" title="Storm">\n        storms\n       </a>\n       that the\n       <a href="/wiki/Westerlies" title="Westerlies">\n        westerlies\n       </a>\n       steer from west to east. Most summer rainfall occurs during\n       <a href="/wiki/Thunderstorm" title="Thunderstorm">\n        thunderstorms\n       </a>\n       and from occasional\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">\n        tropical cyclones\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Humid subtropical climates lie on the east side of continents, roughly between\n       <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">\n        latitudes\n       </a>\n       20\xc2\xb0 and 40\xc2\xb0 degrees away from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">\n        equator\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Koppen_World_Map_Dfa_Dwa_Dsa_Dfb_Dwb_Dsb.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="4231" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Koppen_World_Map_Dfa_Dwa_Dsa_Dfb_Dwb_Dsb.png/220px-Koppen_World_Map_Dfa_Dwa_Dsa_Dfb_Dwb_Dsb.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Koppen_World_Map_Dfa_Dwa_Dsa_Dfb_Dwb_Dsb.png/330px-Koppen_World_Map_Dfa_Dwa_Dsa_Dfb_Dwb_Dsb.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Koppen_World_Map_Dfa_Dwa_Dsa_Dfb_Dwb_Dsb.png/440px-Koppen_World_Map_Dfa_Dwa_Dsa_Dfb_Dwb_Dsb.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Koppen_World_Map_Dfa_Dwa_Dsa_Dfb_Dwb_Dsb.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <center>\n          <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">\n           Humid continental climate\n          </a>\n          ,\n          <a href="/wiki/World" title="World">\n           worldwide\n          </a>\n         </center>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A\n       <b>\n        humid continental\n       </b>\n       climate is marked by variable weather patterns and a large seasonal temperature variance. Places with more than three months of average daily temperatures above 10\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (50\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F) and a coldest month temperature below \xe2\x88\x923\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (27\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F) and which do not meet the criteria for an\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arid_climate" title="Arid climate">\n        arid\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semiarid_climate" title="Semiarid climate">\n        semiarid climate\n       </a>\n       , are classified as continental.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peel2007_31-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Peel2007-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       An\n       <b>\n        oceanic climate\n       </b>\n       is typically found along the west coasts at the middle latitudes of all the world\'s continents, and in southeastern\n       <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">\n        Australia\n       </a>\n       , and is accompanied by plentiful precipitation year-round.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <b>\n        Mediterranean climate\n       </b>\n       regime resembles the climate of the lands in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Basin" title="Mediterranean Basin">\n        Mediterranean Basin\n       </a>\n       , parts of western\n       <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">\n        North America\n       </a>\n       , parts of\n       <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">\n        Western\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Australia" title="South Australia">\n        South Australia\n       </a>\n       , in southwestern\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">\n        South Africa\n       </a>\n       and in parts of central\n       <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">\n        Chile\n       </a>\n       . The climate is characterized by hot, dry summers and cool, wet winters.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A\n       <b>\n        steppe\n       </b>\n       is a dry\n       <a href="/wiki/Grassland" title="Grassland">\n        grassland\n       </a>\n       with an annual temperature range in the summer of up to 40\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (104\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F) and during the winter down to \xe2\x88\x9240\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (\xe2\x88\x9240\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A\n       <b>\n        subarctic climate\n       </b>\n       has little precipitation,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-subritter_35-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-subritter-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and monthly temperatures which are above 10\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (50\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F) for one to three months of the year, with\n       <a href="/wiki/Permafrost" title="Permafrost">\n        permafrost\n       </a>\n       in large parts of the area due to the cold winters. Winters within subarctic climates usually include up to six months of temperatures averaging below 0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (32\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:800px-Map-Tundra.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="370" data-file-width="800" height="102" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/800px-Map-Tundra.png/220px-800px-Map-Tundra.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/800px-Map-Tundra.png/330px-800px-Map-Tundra.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/800px-Map-Tundra.png/440px-800px-Map-Tundra.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:800px-Map-Tundra.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <center>\n          Map of arctic tundra\n         </center>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Tundra\n       </b>\n       occurs in the far\n       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere" title="Northern Hemisphere">\n        Northern Hemisphere\n       </a>\n       , north of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Taiga" title="Taiga">\n        taiga\n       </a>\n       belt, including vast areas of northern\n       <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">\n        Russia\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">\n        Canada\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-berkeley_37-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-berkeley-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A\n       <b>\n        polar ice cap\n       </b>\n       , or polar ice sheet, is a high-\n       <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">\n        latitude\n       </a>\n       region of a\n       <a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">\n        planet\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/Natural_satellite" title="Natural satellite">\n        moon\n       </a>\n       that is covered in\n       <a href="/wiki/Ice" title="Ice">\n        ice\n       </a>\n       . Ice caps form because high-\n       <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">\n        latitude\n       </a>\n       regions receive less energy as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solar_radiation" title="Solar radiation">\n        solar radiation\n       </a>\n       from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">\n        sun\n       </a>\n       than\n       <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">\n        equatorial\n       </a>\n       regions, resulting in lower\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Surface_temperature" title="Surface temperature">\n        surface temperatures\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A\n       <b>\n        desert\n       </b>\n       is a\n       <a href="/wiki/Landscape" title="Landscape">\n        landscape\n       </a>\n       form or region that receives very little\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">\n        precipitation\n       </a>\n       . Deserts usually have a large\n       <a href="/wiki/Diurnal_temperature_variation" title="Diurnal temperature variation">\n        diurnal\n       </a>\n       and seasonal temperature range, with high or low, depending on location daytime temperatures (in summer up to 45\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C or 113\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F), and low nighttime temperatures (in winter down to 0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C or 32\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F) due to extremely low\n       <a href="/wiki/Humidity" title="Humidity">\n        humidity\n       </a>\n       . Many deserts are formed by\n       <a href="/wiki/Rain_shadow" title="Rain shadow">\n        rain shadows\n       </a>\n       , as mountains block the path of moisture and precipitation to the desert.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Thornthwaite">\n        Thornthwaite\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Thornthwaite">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Microthermal" title="Microthermal">\n        Microthermal\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mesothermal" title="Mesothermal">\n        Mesothermal\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Megathermal" title="Megathermal">\n        Megathermal\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MeanMonthlyP.gif">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="744" data-file-width="1200" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/MeanMonthlyP.gif/220px-MeanMonthlyP.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/MeanMonthlyP.gif/330px-MeanMonthlyP.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/MeanMonthlyP.gif/440px-MeanMonthlyP.gif 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MeanMonthlyP.gif" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Precipitation by month\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Devised by the American climatologist and geographer\n       <a href="/wiki/C._W._Thornthwaite" title="C. W. Thornthwaite">\n        C. W. Thornthwaite\n       </a>\n       , this climate classification method monitors the soil water budget using evapotranspiration.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_40-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It monitors the portion of total precipitation used to nourish vegetation over a certain area.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It uses indices such as a humidity index and an aridity index to determine an area\'s moisture regime based upon its average temperature, average rainfall, and average vegetation type.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The lower the value of the index in any given area, the drier the area is.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The moisture classification includes climatic classes with descriptors such as hyperhumid, humid, subhumid, subarid,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semi-arid" title="Semi-arid">\n        semi-arid\n       </a>\n       (values of \xe2\x88\x9220 to \xe2\x88\x9240), and arid (values below \xe2\x88\x9240).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Humid regions experience more precipitation than evaporation each year, while arid regions experience greater evaporation than precipitation on an annual basis. A total of 33\xc2\xa0percent of the Earth\'s landmass is considered either arid or semi-arid, including southwest North America, southwest South America, most of northern and a small part of southern Africa, southwest and portions of eastern Asia, as well as much of Australia.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fredlund1993_44-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Fredlund1993-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Studies suggest that precipitation effectiveness (PE) within the Thornthwaite moisture index is overestimated in the summer and underestimated in the winter.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-greg_45-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-greg-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This index can be effectively used to determine the number of\n       <a href="/wiki/Herbivore" title="Herbivore">\n        herbivore\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Mammal" title="Mammal">\n        mammal\n       </a>\n       species numbers within a given area.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hawkins2004_46-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Hawkins2004-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The index is also used in studies of climate change.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-greg_45-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-greg-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Thermal classifications within the Thornthwaite scheme include microthermal, mesothermal, and megathermal regimes. A microthermal climate is one of low annual mean temperatures, generally between 0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (32\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F) and 14\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (57\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F) which experiences short summers and has a potential evaporation between 14 centimetres (5.5\xc2\xa0in) and 43 centimetres (17\xc2\xa0in).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A mesothermal climate lacks persistent heat or persistent cold, with potential evaporation between 57 centimetres (22\xc2\xa0in) and 114 centimetres (45\xc2\xa0in).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">\n        <a href="#cite_note-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A megathermal climate is one with persistent high temperatures and abundant rainfall, with potential annual evaporation in excess of 114 centimetres (45\xc2\xa0in).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n        <a href="#cite_note-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Record">\n        Record\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Record">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Modern">\n        Modern\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Modern">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Global_Temperature_Anomaly.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="805" data-file-width="951" height="271" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Global_Temperature_Anomaly.svg/320px-Global_Temperature_Anomaly.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Global_Temperature_Anomaly.svg/480px-Global_Temperature_Anomaly.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Global_Temperature_Anomaly.svg/640px-Global_Temperature_Anomaly.svg.png 2x" width="320"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Global_Temperature_Anomaly.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Global mean surface temperature change since 1880. Source:\n         <a class="external text" href="http://data.giss.nasa.gov/gistemp/" rel="nofollow">\n          NASA GISS\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Instrumental_temperature_record" title="Instrumental temperature record">\n        Instrumental temperature record\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Satellite_temperature_measurements" title="Satellite temperature measurements">\n        Satellite temperature measurements\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Details of the modern climate record are known through the taking of measurements from such weather instruments as\n       <a href="/wiki/Thermometer" title="Thermometer">\n        thermometers\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Barometer" title="Barometer">\n        barometers\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Anemometer" title="Anemometer">\n        anemometers\n       </a>\n       during the past few centuries. The instruments used to study weather over the modern time scale, their known error, their immediate environment, and their exposure have changed over the years, which must be considered when studying the climate of centuries past.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Paleoclimatology">\n        Paleoclimatology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Paleoclimatology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Paleoclimatology" title="Paleoclimatology">\n        Paleoclimatology\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Paleoclimatology is the study of past climate over a great period of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">\n        Earth\n       </a>\n       \'s history. It uses evidence from ice sheets, tree rings, sediments, coral, and rocks to determine the past state of the climate. It demonstrates periods of stability and periods of change and can indicate whether changes follow patterns such as regular cycles.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_change">\n        Climate change\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate change">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vostok_Petit_data.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Vostok_Petit_data.svg/220px-Vostok_Petit_data.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Vostok_Petit_data.svg/330px-Vostok_Petit_data.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Vostok_Petit_data.svg/440px-Vostok_Petit_data.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vostok_Petit_data.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Variations in CO\n         <sub>\n          2\n         </sub>\n         , temperature and dust from the\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vostok,_Antarctica" title="Vostok, Antarctica">\n          Vostok\n         </a>\n         ice core over the past 450,000\xc2\xa0years\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">\n        Climate change\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">\n        Global warming\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Temperature_record" title="Temperature record">\n        Temperature record\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Attribution_of_recent_climate_change" title="Attribution of recent climate change">\n        Attribution of recent climate change\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Climate change is the variation in global or regional climates over time. It reflects changes in the variability or average state of the atmosphere over time scales ranging from decades to millions of years. These changes can be caused by processes internal to the Earth, external forces (e.g. variations in sunlight intensity) or, more recently, human activities.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20151128-jg_53-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20151128-jg-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:16-008-NASA-2015RecordWarmGlobalYearSince1880-20160120.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="1920" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/16-008-NASA-2015RecordWarmGlobalYearSince1880-20160120.png/300px-16-008-NASA-2015RecordWarmGlobalYearSince1880-20160120.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/16-008-NASA-2015RecordWarmGlobalYearSince1880-20160120.png/450px-16-008-NASA-2015RecordWarmGlobalYearSince1880-20160120.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/16-008-NASA-2015RecordWarmGlobalYearSince1880-20160120.png/600px-16-008-NASA-2015RecordWarmGlobalYearSince1880-20160120.png 2x" width="300"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:16-008-NASA-2015RecordWarmGlobalYearSince1880-20160120.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <center>\n          2015 \xe2\x80\x93\n          <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">\n           Warmest Global Year\n          </a>\n          on Record (since 1880) \xe2\x80\x93 Colors indicate temperature anomalies (\n          <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n           NASA\n          </a>\n          /\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NOAA" title="NOAA">\n           NOAA\n          </a>\n          ; 20 January 2016).\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20160120_54-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-NASA-20160120-54">\n            [54]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </center>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In recent usage, especially in the context of\n       <a href="/wiki/Environmental_policy" title="Environmental policy">\n        environmental policy\n       </a>\n       , the term "climate change" often refers only to changes in modern climate, including the rise in average surface\n       <a href="/wiki/Temperature" title="Temperature">\n        temperature\n       </a>\n       known as\n       <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">\n        global warming\n       </a>\n       . In some cases, the term is also used with a presumption of human causation, as in the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">\n        United Nations\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNFCCC" title="UNFCCC">\n        Framework Convention on Climate Change\n       </a>\n       (UNFCCC). The UNFCCC uses "climate variability" for non-human caused variations.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">\n        <a href="#cite_note-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Earth has undergone periodic climate shifts in the past, including four major\n       <a href="/wiki/Ice_age" title="Ice age">\n        ice ages\n       </a>\n       . These consisting of glacial periods where conditions are colder than normal, separated by\n       <a href="/wiki/Interglacial" title="Interglacial">\n        interglacial\n       </a>\n       periods. The accumulation of snow and ice during a glacial period increases the surface\n       <a href="/wiki/Albedo" title="Albedo">\n        albedo\n       </a>\n       , reflecting more of the Sun\'s energy into space and maintaining a lower atmospheric temperature. Increases in\n       <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">\n        greenhouse gases\n       </a>\n       , such as by volcanic activity, can increase the global temperature and produce an interglacial period. Suggested causes of ice age periods include the positions of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Continent" title="Continent">\n        continents\n       </a>\n       , variations in the Earth\'s orbit, changes in the solar output, and volcanism.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n        <a href="#cite_note-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_models">\n        Climate models\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate models">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_model" title="Climate model">\n        Climate model\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Climatology" title="Climatology">\n        Climatology\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Climate models use quantitative methods to simulate the interactions of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Earth%27s_atmosphere" title="Earth\'s atmosphere">\n        atmosphere\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n        <a href="#cite_note-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Ocean" title="Ocean">\n        oceans\n       </a>\n       , land surface and ice. They are used for a variety of purposes; from the study of the dynamics of the weather and climate system, to projections of future climate. All climate models balance, or very nearly balance, incoming energy as short wave (including visible) electromagnetic radiation to the earth with outgoing energy as long wave (infrared) electromagnetic radiation from the earth. Any imbalance results in a change in the average temperature of the earth.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The most talked-about applications of these models in recent years have been their use to infer the consequences of increasing greenhouse gases in the atmosphere, primarily\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">\n        carbon dioxide\n       </a>\n       (see\n       <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">\n        greenhouse gas\n       </a>\n       ). These models predict an upward trend in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Surface_temperature_record" title="Surface temperature record">\n        global mean surface temperature\n       </a>\n       , with the most rapid increase in temperature being projected for the higher latitudes of the Northern Hemisphere.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Models can range from relatively simple to quite complex:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        Simple radiant heat transfer model that treats the earth as a single point and averages outgoing energy\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        this can be expanded vertically (radiative-convective models), or horizontally\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        finally, (coupled) atmosphere\xe2\x80\x93ocean\xe2\x80\x93\n        <a href="/wiki/Sea_ice" title="Sea ice">\n         sea ice\n        </a>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_climate_model" title="Global climate model">\n         global climate models\n        </a>\n        discretise and solve the full equations for mass and energy transfer and radiant exchange.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n         <a href="#cite_note-58">\n          [58]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       Climate forecasting is a way by some scientists are using to predict climate change. In 1997 the prediction division of the International Research Institute for Climate and Society at Columbia University began generating seasonal climate forecasts on a real-time basis. To produce these forecasts an extensive suite of forecasting tools was developed, including a multimodel ensemble approach that required thorough validation of each model\'s accuracy level in simulating interannual climate variability.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n       <ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">\n        <li style="display:table-row">\n         <span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cumulus_clouds_in_fair_weather.jpeg">\n           <img alt="icon" class="noviewer" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="24" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Cumulus_clouds_in_fair_weather.jpeg/32px-Cumulus_clouds_in_fair_weather.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Cumulus_clouds_in_fair_weather.jpeg/48px-Cumulus_clouds_in_fair_weather.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Cumulus_clouds_in_fair_weather.jpeg/64px-Cumulus_clouds_in_fair_weather.jpeg 2x" width="32"/>\n          </a>\n         </span>\n         <span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle">\n          <a href="/wiki/Portal:Weather" title="Portal:Weather">\n           Weather portal\n          </a>\n         </span>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">\n
